## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task belongs to chemical kinetics, which is a domain concerned with understanding the rates of chemical reactions and their dependence on various factors such as concentration, temperature, and time. The target variable dA_dt is indicative of reaction rate, and the feature variables t and A are directly related to the temporal and concentration aspects of the reaction.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order rate equation: dA/dt = -k * A (linear decay of concentration)
- Second-order rate equation: dA/dt = -k * A^2 (decay of concentration with non-linear dependence)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA/dt = k_max * A / (K_m + A) (saturated reaction rate with concentration-dependent substrate)
- Hill equation for enzyme-catalyzed reactions: dA/dt = k * A^n / (A^n + K^n) (saturated reaction rate with cooperative substrate binding)
- Catalytic mechanism of enzyme: dA/dt = k_cat * E * S / (K_m + S) (catalyzed reaction with enzyme-dependent rate)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = k_ads * A / (1 + k_ads * A) (adsorption equilibrium on a surface with concentration-dependent rate)
- Beer-Lambert law for reaction rate: dA/dt = k * A * c (reaction rate proportional to concentration and a constant)
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (temperature dependence of reaction rate)
- Catalyst decay over time: dA/dt = k * A / (1 + k * t) (degradation of catalyst with time)
- Reaction activation energy: dA/dt = k * exp(-c * (1 / T - 1 / T_0)) (temperature-dependent reaction rate with activation energy)
- Reaction initiation and termination: dA/dt = k * A * (1 - A / A_max) (simplified model of reaction rate with time-dependent rate constant)
- Kinetics of consecutive reactions: dA/dt = k * A1 * A2 / (1 + k * A1 * A2) (reaction rate with sequential and parallel reactions)
- Bi-exponential decay of concentration: A = c1 * exp(-c2 * t) + c3 * exp(-c4 * t) (two-step reaction process)
- A-variable phase-shift model: A = c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3) (sinusoidal concentration dependence on time)
- Reaction rate with periodic temperature change: dA/dt = k * exp(c * sin(c1 * t)) (temperature-dependent reaction rate with sinusoidal oscillations)
- Unsteady-state concentration in a reactor: dA/dt = -c * A / (1 + c * A) (reactor dynamics with time-dependent reaction rate and concentration)
- Parallel reaction rate model: dA/dt = k * A1 * A2 / (A1 + A2) (reaction rate with multiple reactant species)
- heuristics

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Oscillatory concentration envelope: A(t) = c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * exp(-c4 * t) (decay of oscillatory concentration over time)
- Reaction order with temperature dependence: dA/dt = k * A^c * exp(c1 / T) (reaction rate with non-linear temperature dependence and order c)
- Critical concentration for reaction: dA/dt = k * A / (A^2 + c) (reaction rate with critical concentration for initiation)
- Isothermal reaction rate: dA/dt = k * exp(c * A) (reaction rate with exponential dependence on concentration at constant temperature)
- Double-exponential decay of concentration: dA/dt = k * A * (c1 * exp(-c2 * t) + c3 * exp(-c4 * t)) (decay of concentration with two exponential phases)
- Dynamic steady-state concentration in a reactor: dA/dt = -c * A / (1 + c * A) (reactor dynamics with time-dependent reaction rate and concentration)
- Reaction rate with sensitivity to temperature: dA/dt = k * A * exp(c1 / T - c2 / T_0) (reaction rate with temperature-dependent rate constant and sensitivity to temperature)
- Irreversible reaction with diffusion limitation: dA/dt = -c * A / (1 + c * A) (reaction rate with diffusion limitation and irreversibility)
- Dynamic reaction rate model with hysteresis: dA/dt = k * A * (1 - A / A_max) + c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (reaction rate with hysteresis and time-dependent rate constant)
- Linear combination of reaction rate functions: dA/dt = k1 * A1 + k2 * A2 (reaction rate with weighted sum of multiple reaction components)
